href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_53" title="Puerto Rico Highway 53"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Toll_plate_yellow.svg/25px-Toll_plate_yellow.svg.png" decoding="async" /></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Yabucoa</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;\xca\x9da\xce\xb2u\xcb\x88koa&#93;</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Yabucoa_barrio-pueblo" title="Yabucoa barrio-pueblo">town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> located in the eastern region, north of <a href="/wiki/Maunabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Maunabo, Puerto Rico">Maunabo</a>; south of <a href="/wiki/San_Lorenzo,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Lorenzo, Puerto Rico">San Lorenzo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Las_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="Las Piedras, Puerto Rico">Las Piedras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Humacao, Puerto Rico">Humacao</a>; and east of <a href="/wiki/Patillas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Patillas, Puerto Rico">Patillas</a>. Yabucoa is spread over 9 barrios and <a href="/wiki/Yabucoa_barrio-pueblo" title="Yabucoa barrio-pueblo">Yabucoa Pueblo</a> (the downtown area and the administrative center of the city). It is part of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area">San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area</a>.\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Etymology_and_nicknames">Etymology and nicknames</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and nicknames"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The name <i>Yabucoa</i> is said to come from the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Ta\xc3\xadno language">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> name <i>Guaroca</i>, both a toponymic and personal name meaning "where water [is found]". However this is considered a <a href="/wiki/Folk_etymology" title="Folk etymology">folk etymology</a> and other linguists suggest the name is most likely a <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> interpretation of the Ta\xc3\xadno word <i>yaucoa</i> (similar to the name <a href="/wiki/Yauco,_Puerto_Rico" title="Yauco, Puerto Rico">Yauco</a>) which means "<a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a> plantation".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Some nicknames of the city are "Sugar City", after the numerous sugarcane plantations of the <a href="/wiki/Yabucoa_Valley" title="Yabucoa Valley">Yabucoa Valley</a>, and <i>Pueblo de Yuca</i> ("Yuca Town") which references the Ta\xc3\xadno origin of the name of the town. The locals are also known as the <i>Bebe Leches</i> ("milk drinkers") after the numerous dairy farms located in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The region of what is now Yabucoa belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> region of Guayaney, which covered a portion of the southeast region of Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The region was led by cacique Guaraca. After the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish colonization</a>, the region of Yabucoa belonged to <a href="/wiki/Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Humacao, Puerto Rico">Humacao</a>, and its territory was mostly used for <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a> and farming. Yabucoa, as a town, was founded on October 3, 1793, when Don Manuel Col\xc3\xb3n de Bonilla and his wife, Do\xc3\xb1a Catalina Morales Pacheco, donated the lands to the people.<sup id="cite_ref-enciclopedia_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enciclopedia-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Delgado1878_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Delgado1878-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_2017-09-20_1015Z.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Maria_2017-09-20_1015Z.jpg/220px-Maria_2017-09-20_1015Z.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Maria_2017-09-20_1015Z.jpg/330px-Maria_2017-09-20_1015Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Maria_2017-09-20_1015Z.jpg/440px-Maria_2017-09-20_1015Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1188" data-file-height="792" /></a><figcaption>Maria as it was making landfall near Yabucoa on September 20, 2017</figcaption></figure><figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg/220px-Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg/330px-Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg/440px-Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="770" data-file-height="569" /></a><figcaption>Map of landslides in Puerto Rico caused by Hurricane Maria in 2017</figcaption></figure>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> struck the island of Puerto Rico on September 20, 2017, as a high-end, category 4 hurricane, knocking out power to the entire island and also affected access to clean water. The hurricane made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Camino_Nuevo" title="Camino Nuevo">Camino Nuevo, Yabucoa</a><sup id="cite_ref-ENDI2018_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENDI2018-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and triggered numerous landslides, caused widespread flooding and damaged critical infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Landslides_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Landslides-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Yabucoa\'s municipal buildings sustained mayor damages, and up to 2500 other structures in Yabucoa were affected.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Elderly were especially affected<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> because many homes were completely destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many elderly living in Yabucoa died as a result of Hurricane Maria. People on oxygen machines died with the lack of electrical power. In June, 2018 the administrators of the municipality stated that they noticed an uptick in <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rates" class="mw-redirect" title="Mortality rates">mortality rates</a> (deaths) and were relaying the information since February, of 2018 but the government of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> was not interested in hearing about it. Many more deaths were occurring than expected. An entire new section to the cemetery was built following the hurricane and the deaths that followed.<sup id="cite_ref-CPI_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPI-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>As of June 12, 2018, eight months after the hurricane, more than 30% of Yabucoa homes were still without electrical power, stated the mayor of Yabucoa, Rafael Surillo. He stated there were 4,000 residences with between 12,000 and 15,000 residents without electrical power, of 36,000 residents. Large swaths of Yabucoa municipality including <a href="/wiki/Guayabota" title="Guayabota">Guayabota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tejas,_Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="Tejas, Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">Tejas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Mart%C3%ADn,_Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="Juan Mart\xc3\xadn, Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">Juan Mart\xc3\xadn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calabazas,_Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="Calabazas, Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">Calabazas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Limones,_Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="Limones, Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">Limones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aguacate,_Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguacate, Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">Aguacate</a> barrios, and 100% of <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1canas" title="J\xc3\xa1canas">J\xc3\xa1canas</a> were without electrical power for nine months, some since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a> had hit a week prior to Hurricane Maria.<sup id="cite_ref-CPI_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPI-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jervis_2018_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jervis_2018-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The municipality of Yabucoa is located in the south-eastern coast of Puerto Rico. The <a href="/wiki/Yabucoa_Valley" title="Yabucoa Valley">Valley of Yabucoa</a> is surrounded by the hills of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Lorenzo_Batholith&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="San Lorenzo Batholith (page does not exist)">San Lorenzo Batholith</a> on three sides and by the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> on the fourth. The hills surrounding the Yabucoa Valley as well as the bedrock underlying the alluvium in the valley are composed of the San Lorenzo Batholith, a large, igneous intrusive body emplaced during the <a href="/wiki/Late_Cretaceous" title="Late Cretaceous">Late Cretaceous</a> (Rogers, 1977; Rogers and others, 1979). The San Lorenzo Batholith is a composite body that is composed of <a href="/wiki/Gabbro" title="Gabbro">gabbro</a> (Kd), <a href="/wiki/Diorite" title="Diorite">diorite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tonalite" title="Tonalite">tonalite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Granodiorite" title="Granodiorite">granodiorite</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Quartz_monzonite" title="Quartz monzonite">quartz monzonite</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Pandura" title="Sierra Pandura">Cuchillas de Panduras</a>, a fork of the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Cayey" title="Sierra de Cayey">Sierra de Cayey</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a> runs through its south. Santa Elena is one of its most prominent peaks with an altitude of 1,870 feet (570 meters). Santa Elena is located in Juan Martin ward. Pandura Peak rises 1,693 feet (516 meters) above sea level. Pandura is located in the Calabazas ward. The altitude of the hills surrounding the Valley of Yabucoa reaches a maximum of about 2,130 feet (650 meters) at the head of the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Guayan%C3%A9s" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Guayan\xc3\xa9s">R\xc3\xado Guayan\xc3\xa9s</a> basin. The land surface in the Yabucoa Valley slopes gently from an altitude of about 98 feet (30 meters) above mean sea level, at the western edge of the valley, to sea level where the valley meets the Caribbean Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Yabucoa%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/220px-Yabucoa%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="241" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Yabucoa%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/330px-Yabucoa%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Yabucoa%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/440px-Yabucoa%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="1204" /></a><figcaption>Subdivisions of Yabucoa</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities of Puerto Rico, Yabucoa is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>. The municipal buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in a barrio referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"el pueblo"</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pico_1969_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pico_1969-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-US2010Census_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US2010Census-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;">\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Aguacate,_Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguacate, Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">Aguacate</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Calabazas,_Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="Calabazas, Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">Calabazas</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Camino_Nuevo" title="Camino mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_barrios_and_sectors_of_Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of barrios and sectors of Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">List of barrios and sectors of Yabucoa, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are, in contemporary times, roughly comparable to  <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span> (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Yabucoa: Ingenio, Jacanas Granja, Playa Guayan\xc3\xa9s, Tejas Trinidad, and Urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n Jaime C. Rodr\xc3\xadguez.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wordpress.com_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wordpress.com-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Landmarks and places of interest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li>Guayan\xc3\xa9s Beach and pier<sup id="cite_ref-Victoria840_2019_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Victoria840_2019-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Kyle Rembis beach</li>\n<li>Hacienda Santa Luc\xc3\xada Ruins</li>\n<li>La Casa de la Cultura (House of Culture)</li>\n<li>Roig Refinery</li>\n<li>El Cocal Beach, also known as El Guano Beach</li>\n<li>Public skatepark</li>\n<li><a (and In\xc3\xa9s Mar\xc3\xada Mendoza Nature Reserve)</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Agriculture">Agriculture</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Agriculture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Olein_Recovery_Corp._Yabucoa,_PR_05.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Olein_Recovery_Corp._Yabucoa%2C_PR_05.jpg/220px-Olein_Recovery_Corp._Yabucoa%2C_PR_05.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Olein_Recovery_Corp._Yabucoa%2C_PR_05.jpg/330px-Olein_Recovery_Corp._Yabucoa%2C_PR_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Olein_Recovery_Corp._Yabucoa%2C_PR_05.jpg/440px-Olein_Recovery_Corp._Yabucoa%2C_PR_05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="480" /></a><figcaption>Olein Recovery Corp. in Yabucoa in 2006</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Yabucoa is known for its agricultural prowess because of the surrounding fertile <a href="/wiki/Yabucoa_Valley" title="Yabucoa Valley">valley</a> that produces most of the island\'s <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a>. Yabucoe\xc3\xb1os are known as "sugar people" because most of the valley was used for <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a> growth. In addition, one of the most visible landmarks when entering the municipality is the old Hacienda Roig sugar mill, one of the last mills that produced sugar in Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-PhotoRoig2011_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PhotoRoig2011-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>There\'s an oil recycling company, the only one in the Caribbean, called Olein Recovery Corp. operating in Yabucoa.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Puerto_Rico" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Puerto Rico">COVID-19 pandemic</a> Olein began manufacturing hand sanitizer.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a><figcaption><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Concha Ac\xc3\xbastica To\xc3\xb1o M\xc3\xa1rquez</i></span> in Yabucoa, where community events and concerts are held</figcaption></figure>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Yabucoa celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in September / October. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales de los Santos Angeles Custodios</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Yabucoa include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Sugar Cane Festival - May</li>\n<li>Beach Festival - May</li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Festival del Carmen</i></span> \xe2\x80\x93 July</li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Campesino Festival</i></span> \xe2\x80\x93 October</li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">J\xc3\xadbaro de Martorell Festival</i></span> \xe2\x80\x93 December</li></ul>\n<p>Community events are held at the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Concha Ac\xc3\xbastica To\xc3\xb1o M\xc3\xa1rquez</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_F%C3%A9lix_%22Nacho%22_Mill%C3%A1n_in_Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Estadio_F%C3%A9lix_%22Nacho%22_Mill%C3%A1n_in_Yabucoa%2C_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/220px-Estadio_F%C3%A9lix_%22Nacho%22_Mill%C3%A1n_in_Yabucoa%2C_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Estadio_F%C3%A9lix_%22Nacho%22_Mill%C3%A1n_in_Yabucoa%2C_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/330px-Estadio_F%C3%A9lix_%22Nacho%22_Mill%C3%A1n_in_Yabucoa%2C_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Estadio_F%C3%A9lix_%22Nacho%22_Mill%C3%A1n_in_Yabucoa%2C_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/440px-Estadio_F%C3%A9lix_%22Nacho%22_Mill%C3%A1n_in_Yabucoa%2C_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a><figcaption>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Estadio F\xc3\xa9lix "Nacho" Mill\xc3\xa1n</i></span> stadium, where the Azucareros played their home games, sustained significant damage from Hurricane Maria in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-ENDI_Hurricane_Stadium_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENDI_Hurricane_Stadium-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Azucareros de Yabucoa</i></span> are the <a href="/wiki/Double-A_(baseball)" title="Double-A (baseball)">Double-A (baseball)</a> team of Yabucoa and have won 4 championships. They won the 1994 championship playing against the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Toritos de Cayey</i></span>. In 1995 they won against Cidra and in 1996 they won against Cabo Rojo.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2020, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Azucareros de Yabucoa</i></span> was the eighth Puerto Rico Double-A baseball team to have won 900 games.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Estadio F\xc3\xa9lix "Nacho" Mill\xc3\xa1n</i></span> where the Azucareros played sustained significant damage from Hurricane Maria in 2017 and as of 2020 the stadium remains in disrepair.<sup id="cite_ref-ENDI_Hurricane_Stadium_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENDI_Hurricane_Stadium-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Like all municipalities in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, Yabucoa is administered by a mayor. The current mayor is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rafael_Surillo_Ruiz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rafael Surillo Ruiz (page does not exist)">Rafael Surillo Ruiz</a>, from the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Democratic Party of Puerto Rico">Popular Democratic Party</a> (PPD). Surillo was elected at the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_general_election,_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican general election, 2012">2012 general election</a> and won reelected for his third term in 2020 with 65% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The city belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_VII" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district VII">Puerto Rico Senatorial district VII</a>, which is represented by two Senators. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Su%C3%A1rez_C%C3%A1ceres" title="Jorge Su\xc3\xa1rez C\xc3\xa1ceres">Jorge Su\xc3\xa1rez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Dalmau" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Luis Dalmau">Jos\xc3\xa9 Luis Dalmau</a> were elected as District Senators. A native of Yabucoa <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Luis_Cruz" title="Ram\xc3\xb3n Luis Cruz"> Ram\xc3\xb3n Luis Cruz Burgos</a> was elected to represent the city in those elections.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The design of the flag of Yabucoa is abstract, inspired by the colors of the municipal shield; green, white and violet.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In the shield appear two angels the Santos Angeles Custodios, patron saints of Yabucoa. The color purple (violet) field of the shield represents the highest dignity of the angels. The walking sticks are attributes of the traveller, and refer to the holy office of the Angels as guides and companions in man\'s journey in his earthly life. The canes are adorned with guajana flowers, representing the wealth of the sugar cane. The green land where the angels stand symbolizes the fertile <a href="/wiki/Yabucoa_Valley" title="Yabucoa Valley">valley</a> in which Yabucoa is located.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>One of the main roads to Yabucoa is the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_3" title="Puerto Rico Highway 3">PR-3</a>, which borders the east side of the island. Distance from the capital is approximately 1 hour.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008, a tunnel connecting the town of Yabucoa with the town of <a href="/wiki/Maunabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Maunabo, Puerto Rico">Maunabo</a> was completed.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is currently the longest on the island.\n</p><p>There are 41 bridges in Yabucoa.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_Yabucoe\xc3\xb1os"><span id="Notable_Yabucoe.C3.B1os"></span>Notable <i>Yabucoe\xc3\xb1os</i></h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Notable Yabucoe\xc3\xb1os"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Nydia_Velasquez" class="mw-redirect" title="Nydia Velasquez">Nydia Velasquez</a> - United States congresswoman</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carmen_Delgado_Votaw" title="Carmen Delgado Votaw">Carmen Delgado Votaw</a> (1935\xe2\x80\x932017) - Civil rights activist</li>\n<li>Christian Pag\xc3\xa1n - Winner of <a href="/wiki/Idol_Puerto_Rico" title="Idol Puerto Rico">Idol Puerto Rico</a></li>\n<li>Santiago Vidarte (1828\xe2\x80\x931848) - Poet</li>\n<li>Antonio Ayuso Valdivieso (1899\xe2\x80\x931969) - Politician, lawyer, educator</li>\n<li>Jose Facundo Cintr\xc3\xb3n - Advocated in 1872 and 1873 for the end of slavery.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Emilio_Diaz_Colon" class="mw-redirect" title="Emilio Diaz Colon">Emilio Diaz Colon</a> - member of the military</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Luis_Diaz_Colon" title="Luis Diaz Colon">Luis Diaz Colon</a> -Politician, mayor of Yabucoa</li>\n<li>Jordan A. Caraballo-Vega - Computer Engineer, <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a></li></ul>\n<p>Many residents of Yabucoa have served in the US military service and fought in US wars.<sup id="cite_ref-Veterans_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Veterans-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading
